10:18:30 hoisting in JavaScript refers to the
10:18:32 behavior where a declared variable or a
10:18:34 function is hoisted to the top of the
10:18:37 scope in which they exist during the
10:18:39 compile phase. Now JavaScript has this
10:18:42 behavior. JavaScript has a lot of weird

10:18:48 declared not initialized just declared

10:19:15 of your scope that is it hoists the
10:19:18 variable to the top of whichever
10:19:19 function it is existing. Now there are
10:19:21 three types of hoisting in JavaScript
10:19:24 that is variable hosting function
10:19:26 hoisting and let and con hoisting.

10:19:32 hosting is where only the declarations
10:19:34 are hosted and not their

10:19:45 declaration. But initialization is if

10:19:53 variable not just like x is there. When

11:31:33 server side rendering and how is it
11:31:35 beneficial? Now there is two types of
11:31:37 rendering. One is client side rendering
11:31:39 that is rendering the information after
11:31:42 my local server has fetched the data
11:31:44 from the original server. And the next
11:31:46 one is server sided rendering which is
11:31:49 already delivering to my uh my local
11:31:51 system a rendered web page that is the
11:31:54 in the original server itself the file
11:31:57 will be rendered and then it will be
11:31:58 delivered to my particular local
11:32:00 machine.
11:32:02 Serverside rendering is a technique
11:32:03 where a web page is rendered on the
11:32:05 server before it is sent to the users's
11:32:08 browser. Instead of sending a blank HTML
11:32:11 file with JavaScript code that builds on
11:32:14 the page of the server on the client,
11:32:15 the server generates the HTML with
11:32:17 content already included and sends it to
11:32:20 the browser that is already everything
11:32:22 is defined, everything is rendered and
11:32:23 then the particular data comes to your
11:32:25 local machine that is SSR or serverside
11:32:28 rendering. Now an amazing example of
11:32:30 this is your Times of India website. If
11:32:33 you go to that website and you try to
11:32:34 scroll down, you'll see that all the
11:32:36 data is preloaded for you. How is that
11:32:39 happening? That is called a serverside
11:32:40 rendering because all the data that
11:32:42 you're looking in front of you that is
11:32:44 already rendered. It's not rendering
11:32:45 after it reaches you. It has already
11:32:47 been rendered and then it reaches you.
11:32:50 This significantly reduces your page
11:32:52 loading time. Then another example of
11:32:55 client side rendering is your social
11:32:57 media apps like Instagram. Although
11:32:59 Instagram does uses CSR and SSR
11:33:02 together, the first interface that you
11:33:04 see of Instagram is is serverside
11:33:06 rendering. But once you start scrolling,
11:33:09 it's client side rendering because based
11:33:11 on your user activity, you'll be
11:33:12 suggested that kind of res which you
11:33:15 want to watch at that moment. So that is
11:33:18 client side rendering.
11:33:20 Now the benefits are that it it has a
11:33:23 faster initial load since the HTML is
11:33:25 pre-rendered on the server itself. The
11:33:27 browser can display the content quickly
11:33:29 improving the perceived load time for
11:33:31 the users. Next, better search engine
11:33:34 optimization since the when you when it
11:33:36 is listed down on search engines like
11:33:38 Google and all if it is already rendered
11:33:41 for you then the search engines can look
11:33:43 for certain keywords inside the website.
11:33:45 Now since it is already rendered it is
11:33:47 already there on the website. Hence, it
11:33:48 is easier for the search engines to
11:33:50 locate certain keywords. Search engines
11:33:52 can can easily index the content of
11:33:54 server rendered pages because they don't
11:33:56 need to execute JavaScript to see the
11:33:58 content because it's already there.
11:34:00 Next, improved performance. Since most
11:34:02 of the rendering is done on the server,
11:34:04 client don't need to do as much work to
11:34:06 render the page, which is helpful for
11:34:08 users on slower or less powerful
11:34:10 devices. Reduced interaction time. With
11:34:14 SSR, users can interact with the content
11:34:16 more quickly because they don't have to
